     <!--begin pagefulltext-->
     <div class="page-body pagefulltext">
      <div data-pb-dropzone="main">
       <div class="container">
        <div class="row row-md gutterless o-colset-1-2">
         <div class="col-md-2-3 o-col o-col--primary">
          <a id="mainContent" name="mainContent">
          </a>
          <div data-location="featured_home">
           <ul class="o-curated-area">
            <li class="o-curated-area__col o-curated-area__col--5x">
             <ul class="o-curated-area__col-items">
              <li class="m-article m-article--xxl">
               <a class="m-article__img" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2031738?query=featured_home">
                <span class="m-article__img-container">
                 <img alt="publication image" height="200" sizes="(min-width: 1480px) 560px,
                            (min-width: 1280px) calc(((100vw - 120px) / 12) * 5),
                            (min-width: 1024px) calc(((100vw - 90px) / 12) * 5),
                            (min-width: 768px) calc(((100vw - 70px) / 8) * 5),
                             (min-width: 480px) calc(100vw - 40px),
                            calc(100vw - 32px)" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/large/NEJMoa2031738_600x400-1615830563757.jpg" srcset="/pb-assets/images/editorial/large/NEJMoa2031738_600x400-1615830563757.jpg" width="300"/>
                </span>
               </a>
               <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/original-article">
                Original Article
               </a>
               <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2031738?query=featured_home">
                <b class="m-article__title f-h2">
                 Neutralizing Antibodies to Prevent HIV-1 Infection
                </b>
                <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                 L. Corey and Others
                </em>
                <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                 <p>
                  Two phase 2 trials assessed the efficacy and safety of intravenous infusions of a broadly neutralizing antibody, VRCO1, to prevent HIV-1 infection. VRC01 did not cause adverse events and did not prevent overall HIV-1 acquisition significantly more effectively than placebo. In secondary analyses, VRC01 prevented transmission of VRC01-sensitive HIV-1 isolates.
                 </p>
                </span>
                <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                 Mar 18
                </em>
               </a>
               <p>
                <a class="m-article__related f-related" href="doi/full/10.1056/NEJMe2101131">
                 <strong>
                  Editorial
                 </strong>
                 The AMP Trials  A Glass Half Full
                </a>
               </p>
               <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2031738" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2031738?query=featured_home">

              </li>

             <ul class="o-curated-area__col-items">
              <li class="m-article m-article--m">
               <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/editorial">
                Editorial
               </a>
               <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMe2104584?query=featured_home">
                <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                 Efficacy of Current Covid-19 Vaccines against Variant Viruses
                </b>
                <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                 E.J. Rubin, L.R. Baden, and S. Morrissey
                </em>
                <span class="m-article__img">
                 <span class="m-article__img-container">
                  <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/coronavirus_podcast_300x200-1582749539347.jpg"/>
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                 <p>
                  In this audio interview conducted on March 16, the editors discuss in vitro and clinical results of SARS-CoV-2 vaccination in the setting of viral variants.
                 </p>
                </span>
                <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                 Mar 18
                </em>
               </a>
               <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMe2104584" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMe2104584?query=featured_home">
                <span class="m-article__icons" id="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMe2104584">
                 <svg aria-label="Free Icon." class="icon--free">
                  <use xlink:href="#icon--free">
                  </use>
                 </svg>
                 <svg aria-label="Has Audio Interview." class="icon--audio" data-behavior="ToolTip" data-tooltip="Interview">
                  <use xlink:href="#icon--audio" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">
                  </use>
                 </svg>
                </span>
               </a>
              </li>
              <li class="m-article m-article--m">
               <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/original-article">
                Original Article
               </a>
               <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2102214?query=featured_home">
                <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                 Efficacy of the ChAdOx1 Vaccine against the B.1.351 Variant
                </b>
                <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                 S.A. Madhi and Others
                </em>
                <span class="m-article__img">
                 <span class="m-article__img-container">
                  <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/NEJMoa2102214_300x200-1615922355140.jpg"/>
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                 <p>
                  A double-blind randomized trial in South Africa documented poor efficacy of two doses of the ChAdOx1 nCoV-19 vaccine against the B.1.351 variant of SARS-CoV-2 that emerged in South Africa. Infections occurred in 3.2% of placebo recipients and in 2.5% of vaccine recipients. Thirty-nine of the 42 virus isolates were the B.1.351 variant. None of the cases led to hospitalization or death.
                 </p>
                </span>
                <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                 Mar 16
                </em>
               </a>
               <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2102214" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2102214?query=featured_home">

                 <svg aria-label="Free Icon." class="icon--free">
                  <use xlink:href="#icon--free">
                  </use>
                 </svg>
                </span>
               </a>
              </li>

              <li class="m-article m-article--m">
               <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/correspondence">

               </a>
               <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMc2102179?query=featured_home">
                <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                 Variant SARS-CoV-2 and the mRNA-1273 Vaccine
                </b>
                <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                 K. Wu and Others
                </em>
                <span class="m-article__img">
                 <span class="m-article__img-container">
                  <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/NEJMc2102179_300x200_2-1616004781207.jpg"/>
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                 <p>
                  How well do serum samples from persons vaccinated with the mRNA-1273 vaccine neutralize the P.1 lineage, the B.1.1.7 lineage, the B.1.1.7 lineage plus the E484K mutation, the B.1.351 lineage, and the B.1.427/B.1.429 lineage of SARS-CoV-2? This study provides an answer.
                 </p>
                </span>
                <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                 Mar 17
                </em>
               </a>
               <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMc2102179" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMc2102179?query=featured_home">

               </a>
               <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMp2035905?query=featured_home">
                <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                 New Legislation on Out-of-Network Billing
                </b>
                <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                 K.R. Chhabra, E. Fuse Brown, and A.M. Ryan
                </em>
                <span class="m-article__img">
                 <span class="m-article__img-container">
                  <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/NEJMp2035905_300x200-1616004780897.jpg"/>
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                 <p>
                  The passage of the federal No Surprises Act  which banned surprise billing in many scenarios  was an unexpected step forward. The new legislation will benefit patients and may have little effect on most physicians who dont engage in surprise billing.
                 </p>
                </span>
                <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                 Mar 17
                </em>

               <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMp2032115?query=featured_home">
                <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                 Private Equity and Physician Medical Practices
                </b>
                <em class="m-article__author f-author">

                <em class="m-article__author f-author">

              <li class="m-article m-article--s">
               <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/correspondence">
                Correspondence
               </a>
               <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMc2033943?query=featured_home">
                <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                 Disposable E-Cigarette Use among U.S. Youth
                </b>
                <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                 T.W. Wang and Others
                </em>
                <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                 <p>
                  Despite efforts to curtail the use of e-cigarettes among youth, millions of middle and high school students use them. This study, which compares use in 2019 with use in 2020, shows that despite an overall decline, an increasing percentage of these students report using disposable e-cigarettes.
                 </p>
                </span>
                <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                 Mar 16
                </em>
               </a>
               <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMc2033943" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMc2033943?query=featured_home">
                <span class="m-article__icons" id="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMc2033943">
                 <svg aria-label="Free Icon." class="icon--free">
                  <use xlink:href="#icon--free">
                  </use>
                 </svg>
                </span>
               </a>
              </li>
              <li class="m-article m-article--m">
               <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/original-article">
                Original Article
               </a>
               <span class="m-article__subtype f-caps">
                International Conference on Alzheimers and Parkinsons Diseases
               </span>
               <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2100708?query=featured_home">
                <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                 Trial of an Antibody to Amyloid in Alzheimers Disease
                </b>
                <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                 M.A. Mintun and Others
                </em>
                <span class="m-article__img">
                 <span class="m-article__img-container">
                  <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/NEJMoa2100708_300x200-1615583105547.jpg"/>
                 </span>
                </span>
                <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                 <p>
                  A phase 2 trial of donanemab, an antibody that targets amyloid deposited in the brain, showed a better composite score for cognition and for the ability to perform activities of daily living than placebo at 76 weeks in patients with early Alzheimers disease. Results for secondary outcomes were generally similar in the two trial groups.
                 </p>
                </span>
                <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                 Mar 13
                </em>
               </a>
               <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2100708" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2100708?query=featured_home">

                 <span class="m-article__img-container">
                  <img alt="publication image" height="200" sizes="(min-width: 1480px) 560px,

                <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2032183?query=featured_home">
                 <b class="m-article__title f-h2">
                  Once-Weekly Semaglutide in Adults with Overweight or Obesity
                 </b>
                 <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                  J.P.H. Wilding and Others
                 </em>
                 <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                  <p>
                   This double-blind study randomly assigned adults with obesity (or overweight and with one or more weight-related coexisting conditions) without diabetes to 68 weeks of once-weekly subcutaneous semaglutide (2.4 mg) or placebo, plus lifestyle intervention. Semaglutide therapy was associated with sustained, clinically relevant weight reduction.
                  </p>
                 </span>
                 <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                  Mar 18
                 </em>
                </a>
                <p>
                 <a class="m-article__related f-related" href="doi/full/10.1056/NEJMe2101705">
                  <strong>
                   Editorial
                  </strong>
                  STEP 1 for Effective Weight Control  Another First Step?
                 </a>
                </p>
                <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2032183" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2032183?query=featured_home">
                 <span class="m-article__icons" id="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2032183">
                  <svg aria-label="Has CME." class="icon--cme">

               <li class="m-article m-article--m">
                <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/original-article">
                 Original Article
                </a>
                <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2031893?query=featured_home">
                 <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                  Passive Immunotherapy in Patients with Covid-19
                 </b>
                 <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                  M.J. Joyner and Others
                 </em>
                 <span class="m-article__img">
                  <span class="m-article__img-container">
                   <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/NEJMoa2031893_300x200-1616004911947.jpg"/>
                  </span>
                 </span>
                 <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                  <p>
                   Among more than 3000 hospitalized patients with Covid-19, recipients of high-titer convalescent plasma had a lower mortality at 30 days than recipients of low-titer plasma. The effect of high-titer plasma was greatest in the subgroup of patients who were not receiving mechanical ventilation.
                  </p>
                 </span>
                 <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                  Mar 18
                 </em>
                </a>
                <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2031893" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2031893?query=featured_home">
                 <span class="m-article__icons" id="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2031893">
                  <svg aria-label="Free Icon." class="icon--free">
                   <use xlink:href="#icon--free">
                   </use>
                  </svg>
                  <svg aria-label="Has Visual Abstract." class="icon--visual-abstract-1" data-behavior="ToolTip" data-tooltip="Visual Abstract">
                   <use xlink:href="#icon--visual-abstract-1" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">
                   </use>
                  </svg>
                 </span>
                </a>
               </li>
               <li class="m-article m-article--m">
                <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/original-article">
                 Original Article
                </a>
                <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2029073?query=featured_home">
                 <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                  Inhibition of C3 in Paroxysmal Nocturnal Hemoglobinuria
                 </b>
                 <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                  P. Hillmen and Others
                 </em>
                 <span class="m-article__img">
                  <span class="m-article__img-container">
                   <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/NEJMoa2029073_300x200-1615907517960.jpg"/>
                  </span>
                 </span>
                 <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                  <p>
                   Anemia associated with PNH is caused by hemolysis. The C5 inhibitor eculizumab blocks intravascular hemolysis, but anemia often persists owing to extravascular hemolysis. Pegcetacoplan, an inhibitor of C3, prevents extravascular hemolysis. After 16 weeks of treatment, hemoglobin increased nearly 4 g per deciliter in 41 patients treated with pegcetacoplan, and 85% no longer needed transfusion.
                  </p>
                 </span>
                 <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                  Mar 18
                 </em>
                </a>
                <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2029073" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2029073?query=featured_home">
                 <span class="m-article__icons" id="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMoa2029073">
                  <svg aria-label="Has Quick Take Video." class="icon--video" data-behavior="ToolTip" data-tooltip="Quick Take">

                   </use>
                  </svg>
                 </span>
                </a>
               </li>
              </ul>
             </li>
            </ul>

                  <p>
                   Between October and December 2020, a new SARS-CoV-2 variant (B.1.1.7) rapidly spread across England, including in long-term care facilities.
                  </p>

           <h2 class="a-subtitle" style="margin-bottom:20px;">
            Clinical Practice and Review
           </h2>
           <div data-location="featured_secondary_home">
            <ul class="o-curated-area">
             <li class="o-curated-area__col o-curated-area__col--4x">
              <ul class="o-curated-area__col-items">
               <li class="m-article m-article--m">
                <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/case-records-of-the-massachusetts-general-hospital">
                 Case Records of the Massachusetts General Hospital
                </a>
                <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMcpc2027092?query=featured_home">
                 <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                  A Woman with Cholangiocarcinoma
                 </b>
                 <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                  L. Goyal and Others
                 </em>
                 <span class="m-article__img">
                  <span class="m-article__img-container">
                   <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/NEJMcpc2027092_300x200-1615830579987.jpg"/>
                  </span>
                 </span>
                 <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                  <p>
                   A 34-year-old woman was evaluated in the oncology clinic for the management of recurrent, metastatic intrahepatic cholangiocarcinoma. Before evaluation, an extended right hepatectomy had been performed, and the patient had received adjuvant therapy with gemcitabine and cisplatin. When relapse of the cancer occurred, additional management decisions were made.
                  </p>
                 </span>
                 <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                  Mar 18
                 </em>
                </a>
                <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMcpc2027092" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMcpc2027092?query=featured_home">
                 <span class="m-article__icons" id="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMcpc2027092">
                  <svg aria-label="Has CME." class="icon--cme">
                   <use xlink:href="#icon--cme" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">
                   </use>
                  </svg>
                 </span>
                </a>
               </li>
               <li class="m-article m-article--m">
                <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/clinical-practice">
                 Clinical Practice
                </a>
                <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMcp2019344?query=featured_home">
                 <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                  Epistaxis
                 </b>
                 <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                  H. Seikaly
                 </em>
                 <span class="m-article__img">
                  <span class="m-article__img-container">
                   <img alt="publication image" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/small/NEJMcp2019344_300x200-1615309157690.jpg"/>
                  </span>
                 </span>
                 <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                  <p>
                   Initial management of epistaxis involves digital compression of the lower third of the nose for 15 to 20 minutes. Anterior bleeding not controlled with compression can usually be controlled with topical vasoconstrictors, tranexamic acid, cautery, or anterior nasal packing. If epistaxis continues, posterior packing, arterial ligation, or embolization may be used.
                  </p>
                 </span>
                 <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                  Mar 11
                 </em>
                </a>
                <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMcp2019344" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMcp2019344?query=featured_home">
                 <span class="m-article__icons" id="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMcp2019344">
                  <svg aria-label="Has CME." class="icon--cme">
                   <use xlink:href="#icon--cme" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">
                   </use>
                  </svg>
                  <svg aria-label="Has Full-text Audio." class="icon--audio" data-behavior="ToolTip" data-tooltip="Full Text Audio">
                   <use xlink:href="#icon--audio" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">
                   </use>
                  </svg>
                  <svg aria-label="Has Comments." class="icon--comment" data-behavior="ToolTip" data-tooltip="Comments">
                   <use xlink:href="#icon--comment" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">
                   </use>
                  </svg>
                 </span>
                </a>
               </li>
               <li class="m-article m-article--s">
                <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/perspective">
                 Perspective
                </a>
                <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMp2004154?query=featured_home">
                 <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                  My Intern
                 </b>
                 <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                  R.E. Leiter
                 </em>
                 <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                  <p>
                   Bobby was an intern in our program, and when he and I worked on a team together, he became
                   <em>
                    my
                   </em>
                   intern, and I was
                   <em>
                    his
                   </em>
                   senior resident. By the end of a long, busy month, I was proud of the doctor Bobby had already become. And then one day he didnt come into work.
                  </p>
                 </span>
                 <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                  Mar 18
                 </em>
                </a>
                <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMp2004154" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMp2004154?query=featured_home">
                </a>
               </li>
              </ul>
             </li>
             <li class="o-curated-area__col o-curated-area__col--4x">
              <ul class="o-curated-area__col-items">
               <li class="m-article m-article--l">
                <a class="m-article__img" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMra2033539?query=featured_home">
                 <span class="m-article__img-container">
                  <img alt="publication image" height="200" sizes="(min-width: 1480px) 440px, (min-width: 1280px) calc(((100vw - 420px) / 12) * 4), (min-width: 1024px) calc(((100vw - 100px) / 12) * 4), (min-width: 768px) calc(((100vw - 170px) / 8) * 4), (min-width: 480px) calc(100vw - 40px), calc(100vw - 32px)" src="/pb-assets/images/editorial/large/NEJMra2033539_600x400-1615830564523.jpg" srcset="/pb-assets/images/editorial/large/NEJMra2033539_600x400-1615830564523.jpg" width="300"/>
                 </span>
                </a>
                <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/review-article">
                 Review Article
                </a>
                <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMra2033539?query=featured_home">
                 <b class="m-article__title f-h4">
                  Extrahepatic Manifestations of Chronic HCV Infection
                 </b>
                 <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                  P. Cacoub and D. Saadoun
                 </em>
                 <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                  <p>
                   Hepatitis C virus infection is associated with nonhepatic diseases, including mixed cryoglobulinemic vasculitis, B-cell lymphoma, cardiovascular diseases, type 2 diabetes, and renal dysfunction. Direct-acting antiviral agents that cure the underlying infection are associated with a reduced incidence of most of these diseases.
                  </p>
                 </span>
                 <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                  Mar 18
                 </em>
                </a>
                <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMra2033539" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMra2033539?query=featured_home">
                 <span class="m-article__icons" id="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMra2033539">
                  <svg aria-label="Has CME." class="icon--cme">
                   <use xlink:href="#icon--cme" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">
                   </use>
                  </svg>
                 </span>
                </a>
               </li>
               <li class="m-article m-article--s">
                <a class="m-article__type f-caps" href="/medical-articles/medicine-and-society">
                 Medicine and Society
                </a>
                <a class="m-article__link" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMms2029814?query=featured_home">
                 <b class="m-article__title f-h5">
                  The Political Nature of Sex
                 </b>
                 <em class="m-article__author f-author">
                  K. Slagstad
                 </em>
                 <span class="m-article__blurb f-blurb">
                  <p>
                   Questions about excluding transgender people from antidiscrimination protections reflect the polarizing nature of definitions of sex. Yet historians of medicine know that the relevant moral and scientific questions touch on age-old themes in medical understanding.
                  </p>
                 </span>
                 <em class="m-article__date f-tag">
                  Mar 18
                 </em>
                </a>
                <a aria-labelledby="iconsLabelFor10.1056/NEJMms2029814" href="/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMms2029814?query=featured_home">
                </a>
               </li>
              </ul>
             </li>

                   <span class="m-result__main">

                    </b>
                    <br/>
                    <em class="m-result__author f-author">
                     A. Desmond and P.A. Offit
                    </em>
